
I N D E X
THE terminology and arrangement of the index reflect two assumptions. First, Thomas Jefferson, even beyond his own entry, is the primum mobile. If bacon is "bought," he did the buying; if buildings are "measured," he carried the tape measure. Secondly, places without indications of state or country are assumed to be in Virginia.
  A work that mentions almost every conceivable object for sale during the sixty years of Jefferson's daily recordkeeping called out for  an  ordering  hand.  Inani­ mate objects appear, not in their alphabetical position with  names,  but  grouped under broad subject headings. The titles of books, pamphlets, newspapers, and periodicals also do not apper alphabetically but are grouped under appropriate headings. Taverns and ferries appear  both  in  their  alphabetical  position  and  un­ der  appropriate  headings  grouped  by  state,  city,  or river.
The subject headings are: Agriculture
Animals
Art  and Architecture
Books, Pamphlets, and Maps Building Operations and Materials Clothing
Coins and Currency Ferries
Food and Drink Furnishings  and Furniture
Horses, Mules, and Saddlery Horticulture
Household Articles Medical Subjects
Mills and Manufactures Miscellaneous Articles, with sub-
headings: Firearms
Hardware
Instruments and Machines Leather
Personal Articles Postage
Tools Watches
Music
Newspapers and Periodicals Roads  and Canals
Servants Slaves
Taverns, Hotels, and Ordinaries Textiles
Vehicles
Writing Equipment
